A rite for adoration of the crucified Christ includes the optional singing of the Solemn Reproaches in an updated and revised translation which eliminates some of the anti-Jewish overtones in previous versions. Many Lutheran churches have Good Friday services, such as the <a href="/wiki/Three_Hours%27_Agony" title="Three Hours' Agony">Three Hours' Agony</a> centered on the remembrance of the "Seven Last Words," sayings of Jesus assembled from the four gospels, while others hold a liturgy that places an emphasis on the triumph of the cross, and a singular biblical account of the Passion narrative from the Gospel of John.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Along with observing a general Lenten fast,<sup id="cite_ref-GassmannOldenburg2011_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GassmannOldenburg2011-83">[83]</a></sup> many Lutherans emphasize the importance of Good Friday as a day of fasting within the kalendar.<sup id="cite_ref-Pfatteicher1990_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pfatteicher1990-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JacobsHaas1899_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JacobsHaas1899-7">[7]</a></sup> <i>A Handbook for the Discipline of Lent</i> recommends the Lutheran guideline to "Fast on Ash Wednesday and Good Friday with only one simple meal during the day, usually without meat".<sup id="cite_ref-ELCA1978_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ELCA1978-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Methodist_Church">Methodist Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Methodist Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg/220px-Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg/330px-Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg/440px-Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="4032"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A United Methodist minister <a href="/wiki/Prostration" title="Prostration">prostrates</a> at the start of the Good Friday liturgy at Holy Family Church, in accordance with the rubrics in the <a href="/wiki/The_United_Methodist_Book_of_Worship_(1992)" title="The United Methodist Book of Worship (1992)">Book of Worship</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Processional_cross" title="Processional cross">processional cross</a> is veiled in black, the liturgical colour associated with Good Friday in Methodist Churches.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg/350px-Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg/525px-Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg/700px-Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="1960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>On Maundy Thursday, the <a href="/wiki/Stripping_of_the_Altar" title="Stripping of the Altar">altar of this Methodist church was stripped</a> and the crucifix of this Methodist church has been veiled in black for Good Friday (black is the liturgical colour for Good Friday in the United Methodist Church). A wooden cross sits in front of the bare chancel for the veneration of the cross ceremony, which occurs during the United Methodist Good Friday liturgy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Many <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodist denominations</a> commemorate Good Friday with fasting,<sup id="cite_ref-BaysWacker2010_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaysWacker2010-86">[86]</a></sup> as well as a <a href="/wiki/Service_of_worship" class="mw-redirect" title="Service of worship">service of worship</a> based on the Seven Last Words from the Cross; this liturgy is known as the <a href="/wiki/Three_Hours%27_Agony" title="Three Hours' Agony">Three Hours Devotion</a> as it starts at noon and concludes at 3 pm, the latter being the time that Jesus died on the cross.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reflector-Good_Friday_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reflector-Good_Friday-88">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moravian_Church">Moravian Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Moravian Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">Moravians</a> hold a <a href="/wiki/Lovefeast" class="mw-redirect" title="Lovefeast">Lovefeast</a> on Good Friday as they receive Holy Communion on Maundy Thursday. </p>
      <p>Communicants of the Moravian Church practice the Good Friday tradition of cleaning <a href="/wiki/God%27s_Acre" title="God's Acre">gravestones in Moravian cemeteries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ2020_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ2020-9">[9]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reformed_Churches">Reformed Churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Reformed Churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> tradition, Good Friday is one of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_feast" title="Evangelical feast">evangelical feasts</a> and is thus widely observed with <a href="/wiki/Church_service" title="Church service">church services</a>, which feature the Solemn Reproaches in the pattern of <a href="/wiki/Psalm_78" title="Psalm 78">Psalm 78</a>, towards the end of the liturgy.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Christian_traditions">Other Christian traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other Christian traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>It is not uncommon for some communities to hold <a href="/wiki/Ecumenism" title="Ecumenism">interdenominational</a> services on Good Friday. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Associated_customs">Associated customs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Associated customs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg/220px-Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg/330px-Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg/440px-Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1872"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Good Friday service in Ireland
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In many countries with a strong Christian tradition such as Australia, Bermuda, Brazil, Canada, the countries of the Caribbean, Chile, Colombia, Costa Rica, Czech Republic, Ecuador, Finland, Germany, Hungary, Malta, Mexico, New Zealand,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Peru, the Philippines, Portugal, the Scandinavian countries, Singapore, Spain, Switzerland, the United Kingdom, and Venezuela, the day is observed as a <a href="/wiki/List_of_holidays_by_country" title="List of holidays by country">public or federal holiday</a>. In the United States, 12 states observe Good Friday as state holiday: Connecticut, Texas, Delaware, Hawaii, Indiana, Tennessee, Florida, Kentucky, Louisiana, New Jersey, North Carolina and North Dakota. One associated custom is strict adherence to the Black Fast to 3pm or 6pm,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> where only water can be consumed or restricted handout of bread, herbs and salt. St. Ambrose, St. Chrysostom and St. Basil attest to the practice. The processions of the day, hymns "Crux fidelis" by King John of Portugal, and Eberlin's "Tenebrae factae sunt", followed by "Vexilla Regis" is sung, translated from Latin as <i>the standards of the King advance</i>, and then follows a ceremony that is not a real Mass, it is called the "Mass of the Pre-Sanctified.". This custom is respected also by forgoing the Mass, this is to take heed to the solemnity of the Sacrifice of Calvary. This is where the host of the prior day is placed at the altar, incensed, elevated so "that it may be seen by the people" and consumed. Germany and some other countries have laws prohibiting certain acts, such as dancing and horse racing, that are seen as profaning the solemn nature of the day.<sup id="cite_ref-Petre_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petre-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stevens_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stevens-95">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia_and_New_Zealand">Australia and New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Australia and New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Good Friday is a holiday under state and territory laws in all states and territories in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Generally speaking, shops in all Australian states (but not in the two territories of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory" title="Australian Capital Territory">Australian Capital Territory</a>) are required to remain closed for the duration of Good Friday, although there are certain shops which are permitted to open and other shops can apply for exemptions. All schools and universities close on Good Friday in Australia, and Good Friday falls within the school holidays in most years in all states and territories except the Northern Territory, although many states now commence their school holidays in early April regardless of Easter. In 2018, for example, when Good Friday fell on 30 March, only <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> had school holidays which coincided with Good Friday.<sup id="cite_ref-australia.gov.au/about-australia/special-dates-and-events/school-term-dates_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-australia.gov.au/about-australia/special-dates-and-events/school-term-dates-97">[97]</a></sup> The vast majority of businesses are closed on Good Friday, although many recreational businesses, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Royal_Easter_Show" title="Sydney Royal Easter Show">Sydney Royal Easter Show</a>, open on Good Friday as among non-religious families Good Friday is a popular day to indulge in such activities. In New Zealand, Good Friday is a legal holiday<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> and is a day of mandatory school closure for all New Zealand state and integrated schools.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Good Friday is also a restricted trading day in New Zealand, which means that unexempted shops are not permitted to open on this day.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_(2010).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg/220px-Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg/330px-Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg/440px-Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3052"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_(2010).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="#Vespers_of_Holy_and_Great_Friday">Vespers of Good Friday afternoon</a>, Greek Orthodox Cathedral in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Canada, Good Friday is a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Canada" title="Public holidays in Canada">federal statutory holiday</a>. In the province of Quebec "employers can choose to give the day off either on Good Friday or Easter Monday."<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In an online article posted on <a href="/wiki/Catholic_News_Agency" title="Catholic News Agency">Catholic News Agency</a> by Alejandro Bermúdez on 31 March 2012, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Cuba" title="President of Cuba">Cuban President</a> <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Castro" title="Raúl Castro">Raúl Castro</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="Communist Party of Cuba">Communist Party</a> and his advisers, decreed that Good Friday that year would be a holiday. This was Castro's response to a request made personally to him by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> during the latter's Apostolic Visitation to the island and <a href="/wiki/Leon,_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Leon, Mexico">León</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> that month. The move followed the pattern of small advances in Cuba's relations with the Vatican, mirroring Pope John Paul II's success in getting <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> to declare <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas Day">Christmas Day</a> a holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Both Good Friday and Christmas are now <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Cuba" title="Public holidays in Cuba">annual holidays in Cuba</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, Good Friday was designated a public holiday in the Holidays Ordinance, 1875.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Good Friday continues to be a holiday after the <a href="/wiki/Handover_of_Hong_Kong" title="Handover of Hong Kong">transfer of sovereignty from the UK to China</a> in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Government offices, banks, post offices and most offices are closed on Good Friday. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, Good Friday is not an official public holiday, but most non-retail businesses close for the day. Up until 2018 it was illegal to sell alcoholic beverages on Good Friday, with some exceptions, so pubs and off-licences generally closed.<sup id="cite_ref-ie-wheretolook_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ie-wheretolook-105">[105]</a></sup> Critics of the ban included the catering and tourism sector, but surveys showed that the general public were divided on the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-independent-goodfridayalcohol_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent-goodfridayalcohol-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, a similar ban operates until 5&nbsp;pm on Good Friday.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-restrictionsni_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-restrictionsni-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Although Malaysia is a <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim majority country</a>, Good Friday is declared as a public holiday in the states of <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Malaysia" title="East Malaysia">East Malaysia</a> as there is a significant Christian indigenous population in both states.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malta">Malta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Malta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_ZebbugM_-_Good_Friday_202_ies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Malta_-_ZebbugM_-_Good_Friday_202_ies.jpg/170px-Malta_-_ZebbugM_-_Good_Friday_202_ies.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Malta_-_ZebbugM_-_Good_Friday_202_ies.jpg/255px-Malta_-_ZebbugM_-_Good_Friday_202_ies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Malta_-_ZebbugM_-_Good_Friday_202_ies.jpg/340px-Malta_-_ZebbugM_-_Good_Friday_202_ies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="5616"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_ZebbugM_-_Good_Friday_202_ies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Holy_Week_procession" title="Holy Week procession">Holy Week procession</a> in Malta
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Holy Week commemorations reach their peak on Good Friday as the Roman Catholic Church celebrates the passion of Jesus. Solemn celebrations take place in all churches together with processions in different villages around <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>. During the celebration, the narrative of the passion is read in some localities, while the Adoration of the Cross follows. Good Friday processions take place in <a href="/wiki/Birgu" title="Birgu">Birgu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bormla" class="mw-redirect" title="Bormla">Bormla</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7axaq" title="Għaxaq">Għaxaq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luqa" title="Luqa">Luqa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mosta" title="Mosta">Mosta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naxxar" title="Naxxar">Naxxar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paola,_Malta" title="Paola, Malta">Paola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qormi" title="Qormi">Qormi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabat" title="Rabat">Rabat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senglea" title="Senglea">Senglea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBebbu%C4%A1,_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="Żebbuġ, Malta">Żebbuġ (Città Rohan)</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBejtun" title="Żejtun">Żejtun</a>. Processions in Gozo will be in <a href="/wiki/Nadur" title="Nadur">Nadur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Gozo" title="Victoria, Gozo">Victoria</a> (St. George and Cathedral), <a href="/wiki/Xag%C4%A7ra" title="Xagħra">Xagħra</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBebbu%C4%A1,_Gozo" title="Żebbuġ, Gozo">Żebbuġ, Gozo</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the predominantly <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in the Philippines">Roman Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, the day is commemorated with street processions, the <a href="/wiki/Way_of_the_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Way of the Cross">Way of the Cross</a>, the chanting of the <i><a href="/wiki/Pasyon" title="Pasyon">Pasyón</a></i>, and performances of the <i>Senákulo</i> or <a href="/wiki/Passion_play" class="mw-redirect" title="Passion play">Passion play</a>. Some devotees engage in self-<a href="/wiki/Flagellant" title="Flagellant">flagellation</a> and even have themselves <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_in_the_Philippines" title="Crucifixion in the Philippines">crucified</a> as expressions of penance despite health risks and strong disapproval from the Church.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Church bells are not rung and Masses are not celebrated, while television features movies, documentaries and other shows focused on the religious event and other topics related to the Catholic faith, broadcasting mostly religious content. Malls and shops are generally closed, as are restaurants as it is the second of three public holidays within the week.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>After three o'clock in the afternoon (the time at which Jesus is traditionally believed to have died), the faithful venerate the cross in the local church and follow the procession of the Burial of Jesus. </p>
      <p>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a> and many parts of the <a href="/wiki/Visayan_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Visayan Islands">Visayan Islands</a>, people usually eat <i><a href="/wiki/Binignit" title="Binignit">binignit</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Philippines#Merienda" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of the Philippines">biko</a></i> as a form of fasting.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nazarenosblancos.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Nazarenosblancos.jpg/170px-Nazarenosblancos.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Nazarenosblancos.jpg/255px-Nazarenosblancos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Nazarenosblancos.jpg/340px-Nazarenosblancos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1012" data-file-height="1546"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nazarenosblancos.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nazarenos wearing <a href="/wiki/Capirote" title="Capirote">capirotes</a>, in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">Málaga</a>, Spain
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hot_cross_bun.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hot_cross_bun.jpg/220px-Hot_cross_bun.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hot_cross_bun.jpg/330px-Hot_cross_bun.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hot_cross_bun.jpg/440px-Hot_cross_bun.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hot_cross_bun.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hot_cross_bun" title="Hot cross bun">Hot cross buns</a> are traditionally toasted and eaten on Good Friday in Britain, Canada, Australia and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/UK" class="mw-redirect" title="UK">UK</a>, Good Friday was historically a common law holiday and is recognised as an official public holiday<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> (also known as a <a href="/wiki/Bank_Holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank Holiday">Bank Holiday</a>). All state schools are closed and most businesses treat it as a holiday for staff; however, many retail stores now remain open. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Civil_Service" title="Northern Ireland Civil Service">Government</a> services in Northern Ireland operate as normal on Good Friday, substituting <a href="/wiki/Easter_Tuesday" title="Easter Tuesday">Easter Tuesday</a> for the holiday. </p>
      <p>There has traditionally been no horse racing on Good Friday in the UK. However, in 2008, betting shops and stores opened for the first time on this day<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> and in 2014 Lingfield Park and Musselburgh staged the UK's first Good Friday race meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> has for many years introduced its 7&nbsp;am News broadcast on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">Radio 4</a> on Good Friday with a verse from <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Watts" title="Isaac Watts">Isaac Watts</a>' hymn "<a href="/wiki/When_I_Survey_the_Wondrous_Cross" title="When I Survey the Wondrous Cross">When I Survey the Wondrous Cross</a>". </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, Good Friday is not a government holiday at the federal level; however, individual states, counties and municipalities may observe the holiday. Good Friday is a state holiday in <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a> (half-day),<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> State and local government offices and courts are closed, as well as some banks and post offices in these states, and in those counties and municipalities where Good Friday is observed as a holiday. Good Friday is also a holiday in the U.S. territories of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The stock markets are closed on Good Friday,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> but the foreign exchange and bond trading markets open for a partial business day.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Most retail stores remain open, while some of them may close early. Public schools and universities are often closed on Good Friday, either as a holiday of its own, or as part of <a href="/wiki/Spring_break" title="Spring break">spring break</a>. The postal service operates, and banks regulated by the federal government do not close for Good Friday.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In some governmental contexts Good Friday has been referred to by a generic name such as "spring holiday".<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> In 1999, in the case of <i>Bridenbaugh v. O'Bannon</i>, an Indiana state employee sued the governor for giving state employees Good Friday as a day off. The US Seventh Circuit Court of Appeals ruled against the plaintiff, stating that the government could give state employees a paid day off when that day is a religious holiday, including Good Friday, but only so long as the state can provide a valid secular purpose that coincides with the obvious religious purpose of the holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Calculating_the_date">Calculating the date</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Calculating the date">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

      <p>Good Friday is the Friday before Easter, which is calculated differently in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">Eastern Christianity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Computus" class="mw-redirect" title="Computus">Computus</a> for details). Easter falls on the first Sunday following the Paschal Full Moon, the full moon on or after 21 March, taken to be the date of the vernal <a href="/wiki/Equinox" title="Equinox">equinox</a>. The Western calculation uses the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian calendar</a>, while the Eastern calculation uses the <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian calendar</a>, whose 21 March now corresponds to the Gregorian calendar's 3 April. The calculations for identifying the date of the full moon also differ.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In Eastern Christianity, Easter can fall between 22 March and 25 April on Julian Calendar (thus between 4 April and 8 May in terms of the Gregorian calendar, during the period 1900 and 2099), so Good Friday can fall between 20 March and 23 April, inclusive (or between 2 April and 6 May in terms of the Gregorian calendar).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tnone">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lent_calendar.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Lent_calendar.svg/400px-Lent_calendar.svg.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Lent_calendar.svg/600px-Lent_calendar.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Lent_calendar.svg/800px-Lent_calendar.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="256"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lent_calendar.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Good Friday</i> and other named days and day ranges around Lent and Easter in Western Christianity, with the fasting days of Lent numbered
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_references">Cultural references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Cultural references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Good Friday assumes a particular importance in the plot of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Richard Wagner</a>'s music drama <i><a href="/wiki/Parsifal" title="Parsifal">Parsifal</a></i>, which contains an orchestral interlude known as the "Good Friday Music".<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Practices_of_non-observers">Practices of non-observers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Practices of non-observers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Some <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a> congregations,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Church_of_God" title="Philadelphia Church of God">Philadelphia Church of God</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> and some <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-denominational Christianity">non-denominational</a> churches oppose the observance of Good Friday, regarding it as a so-called <a href="/wiki/Papist" class="mw-redirect" title="Papist">papist</a> tradition, and instead observe the <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">Crucifixion of Jesus</a> on Wednesday to coincide with the Jewish sacrifice of the Passover Lamb (which some/many Christians believe is an Old Testament pointer to Jesus Christ). A Wednesday Crucifixion of Jesus allows for him to be in the tomb ("heart of the earth") for three days and three nights as he told the Pharisees he would be (Matthew 12:40), rather than two nights and a day (by <a href="/wiki/Counting#Inclusive_counting" title="Counting">inclusive counting</a>, as was the norm at that time) if he had died on a Friday.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Preparation Day (14 <a href="/wiki/Nisan" title="Nisan">Nisan</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_calendar" title="Hebrew calendar">Hebrew calendar</a>) – which is the day before Passover (15 Nisan), instead of the Friday morning as the <a href="/wiki/Synoptic_Gospel" class="mw-redirect" title="Synoptic Gospel">Synoptic Gospels</a> refer to the sabbath and they believe this refers to a "high sabbath" (John 19:31) which occurs on feast days, and not the ordinary weekly sabbath. </p>
      <p>Further support for a Wednesday crucifixion based on Matthew 12:40 includes the Jewish belief that death was not considered official until the beginning of the fourth day, which is disallowed with the traditional Friday afternoon to Sunday morning period of time. As "the Jews require a sign" (1 Corinthians 1:22), the resurrection of Christ is thus invalidated with the shorter interval, since it can thus be claimed that Christ could have only 'swooned,' rather than actually died. Additional rationale includes Daniel's statement concerning the "sacrifice and the oblation to cease" (Daniel 9:27) "in the midst of the week," the middle day of the week being Wednesday. This occurred when the vail in the temple was torn in two (Matthew 27:51). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

         <li id="cite_note-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-37">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There is a wide variety of uses regarding the <a href="/wiki/Liturgical_colors" class="mw-redirect" title="Liturgical colors">liturgical colors</a> worn during Great Lent and Holy Week in the Rite of Constantinople.</span> </li>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFRobert_Barron" class="citation web cs1"><a href="/wiki/Robert_Barron_(bishop)" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Barron (bishop)">Robert Barron</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.wofdigital.org/tre-ore-the-three-hours-agony">"Tre Ore - The Three Hours' Agony"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Word_on_Fire" title="Word on Fire">Word on Fire</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">18 April</span> 2019</span>. <q>'The Three Hours' Agony' or Tre Ore is a liturgical service held on Good Friday from noon until 3 o'clock to commemorate the Passion of Christ. Specifically, it refers to the three hours that Jesus hung on the Cross and includes a series of homilies on the seven last words spoken by Christ.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Tre+Ore+-+The+Three+Hours%27+Agony&amp;rft.pub=Word+on+Fire&amp;rft.au=Robert+Barron&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.wofdigital.org%2Ftre-ore-the-three-hours-agony&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGood+Friday" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>

Scarecrow Press. p.&nbsp;229. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0810874824" title="Special:BookSources/978-0810874824"><bdi>978-0810874824</bdi></a>. <q>In many Lutheran churches, the Sundays during the Lenten season are called by the first word of their respective Latin Introitus (with the exception of Palm/Passion Sunday): Invocavit, Reminiscere, Oculi, Laetare, and Judica. Many Lutheran church orders of the 16th century retained the observation of the Lenten fast, and Lutherans have observed this season with a serene, earnest attitude. Special days of eucharistic communion were set aside on Maundy Thursday and Good Friday.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Historical+Dictionary+of+Lutheranism&amp;rft.pages=229&amp;rft.pub=Scarecrow+Press&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.isbn=978-0810874824&amp;rft.aulast=Gassmann&amp;rft.aufirst=G%C3%BCnther&amp;rft.au=Oldenburg%2C+Mark+W.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGood+Friday" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
